The Second Objection: Islamic Law Criterion Excludes Mistaken Theologians
Al-Sharh presents the second objection with sectarian examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the condition of following Islamic law fails to distinguish kalam from non-kalam, as it would exclude the very people considered part of the discipline.

Core Idea
The Islamic law criterion backfires: it excludes mistaken theologians who are undeniably part of kalam.

In this passage, al-Sharh presents the second major objection to defining kalam's subject as research according to Islamic law. The objection shows that if we take 'law of Islam' to mean only true doctrine, then all false doctrines would be excluded, yet even heretical theologians are considered practitioners of kalam. This forces a refinement of the criterion.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and its logical structure
Read the Arabic passage once to grasp the flow: the stated condition, the problem it creates, and the examples. Notice how the objection is constructed.
The objection uses a reductio: if law of Islam = true issues only, then false issues are excluded, but mistaken theologians are part of kalam.
2
Identify the examples and their significance
Spot the mentions of al-mujassima and al-Mu'tazila. Why are they used? They represent groups that are clearly mistaken (even declared disbelievers) yet their issues are still within kalam.
The examples reinforce that the criterion is too narrow.
3
Reflect on the implication for the definition
Consider: if the definition of kalam requires research according to Islamic law in the sense of true doctrine, then these groups would be excluded. But they are not. So the definition fails.
This sets up the need for an answer in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(الثاني قانون الإسلام ما هو الحق من المسائل الكلامية إذ المسائل الباطلة خارجة عن قانون الإسلام قطعاً فإن زعم القائل أن الكلام هو هذه المسائل الحقة فقط ورد عليه ما أشار إليه بقوله ( وبهذا القدر) أي بكون المسائل حقة على قانون الإسلام ) لا يتميز العلم ) أي علم الكلام عما ليس علم الكلام كيف وكل من صاحبي المسائل الحقة والباطلة ( يدعي ذلك ) أي كون مسائله حقة على قانون الإسلام (مع أن هذا الزعم منه باطل قطعاً، لأن ( المخطئ من أرباب علم (الكلام ومسائله من مسائل ،الكلام، كما أشير إليه بقوله ( وإن كفر) ذلك المخطئ كالمجسمة المصرحين بكونه تعالى جسماً، دون القائلين باتصافه بصفات الأجسام المتسترين بالبلكفة ( أو بدع) كالمعتزلة وقد يجاب عنه بأن المراد بكون البحث على قانون الإسلام أن تلك المسائل مأخوذة من الكتاب قوله: ( الثانى قانون إلخ حاصله أن هذا القيد وإن أفاد امتيازه عن الإلهي، لكنه مخل بالتعريف لأن قانون الإسلام إنما هو المسائل الحقة، فيلزم خروج مسائل المخطئ عن الكلام، وهو خلاف المقرر عندهم، وإن التزم مخالفة القوم يلزم عدم امتيازه عما ليس بكلام أعني مسائل المخطئ لأنه أيضاً يدعي أنها حقة، والجواب أن قانون الإسلام ما هو الحق، ولو بزعم الزاعم فيشمل مسائل المخطئ. قوله : (بالبلكفة) مأخوذ من بلا ،كيفية أي المستترين بنفي الكيفية حيث يقولون : أنه تعالى مستو على العرش لا كاستوائنا له وله وجه ويد لا كوجهنا ويدنا، وفي بعض النسخ بالكيفية فالباء للتعدية أي السائرين للكيفية. قوله : ( مأخوذة من الكتاب لعل مراده بالأخذ أن يحافظ في جميع تلك المباحث على القواعد الشرعية، ولا يخالف القطعية منها في اعتقاده فلا يرد أنه إذا لم يكن المخطئ مخالفاً للمسائل القطعية لا يصح تكفيره لأن من يكفره يعتقد أنه مخالف للقطعية، وإن لم يكن قوله : (مع أن هذا الزعم منه (باطل لا يقال : المراد بالحق أعم مما في نفس الأمر وعند الزاعم لأنا نقول : إذا أريد بقانون الإسلام ما هو الحق، وعمم الحق لكلا القسمين لم يحصل المطلوب وهو خروج الإلهي لأن صاحبه أيضاً يدعي حقيته.
The second: 'the law of Islam is that which is true from theological issues (al-masa'il al-kalamiyya), since false issues are definitely outside the law of Islam. For if the claimant says that kalam is only these true issues, he is refuted by what he himself indicated by his saying: 'And to this extent', i.e., by the issues being true according to the law of Islam, 'the science (i.e., the science of kalam) is not distinguished' from what is not the science of kalam. How so? For both the proponent of true issues and the proponent of false issues 'claim that', i.e., that his issues are true according to the law of Islam, while this claim of his is definitely false, because 'the mistaken one among the masters of the science of kalam and his issues are from the issues of kalam', as is indicated by his saying: 'even if that mistaken one disbelieves' like the anthropomorphists (al-mujassima) who explicitly say that God is a body, unlike those who say He is described with attributes of bodies while concealing themselves by negating modality (al-balkafa), or innovators (bida') like the Mu'tazila. And it may be answered that what is meant by research being according to the law of Islam is that those issues are taken from the Book. His saying: 'The second: law, etc.' The gist of it is that this condition, although it distinguishes it from divine philosophy, yet it impairs the definition because the law of Islam is only the true issues, so it necessitates the exclusion of the mistaken person's issues from kalam, which contradicts what is established among them. And if one insists on opposing the school, it entails that it is not distinguished from what is not kalam, i.e., the mistaken person's issues, because he also claims they are true. And the answer is that the law of Islam is that which is true, even if by the claimant's claim, so it includes the mistaken person's issues. His saying: 'by al-balkafa' is derived from 'bila kayfiyya' (without modality), i.e., those who conceal themselves by negating modality, saying: He, exalted, is established on the Throne not like our establishment, and He has a face and hand not like our face and hand. In some copies it is 'bil-kayfiyya', so the ba' is for transitive, i.e., those who walk in modality. His saying: 'taken from the Book' perhaps he means by 'taking' that he preserves in all those investigations the legal principles, and does not violate the definitive ones among them in his belief, so it is not objected that if the mistaken one does not violate definitive issues, his disbelief is not valid, because the one who declares him disbeliever believes he is violating definitive issues, even if he is not. His saying: 'while this claim of his is false' it is not said: the intended meaning of truth is more general than what is in reality and what is according to the claimant's view, for we say: if what is meant by the law of Islam is that which is true, and truth is generalized to both kinds, the objective is not attained, namely the exclusion of divine philosophy, because its proponent also claims its truth.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage deals with the second objection to the definition of kalam's subject. The objection argues that if the distinguishing feature of kalam is that its research follows the law of Islam (qanun al-Islam), then since the law of Islam is only true issues (al-masa'il al-haqqa), false issues would be excluded from kalam. But even a mistaken theologian (al-mukhti') still belongs to the science of kalam, and his issues are considered kalam issues, as indicated by the author's words 'even if that mistaken one disbelieves'. Examples are anthropomorphists (al-mujassima) and innovators like the Mu'tazila. Therefore, the condition of Islamic law does not distinguish kalam from non-kalam, because both the true and the false claim their views are according to Islamic law. The commentator (al-Sharh) explains the objection: the condition helps distinguish from philosophy but undermines the definition because it would exclude mistaken views. He then offers an answer: the law of Islam is understood as what is true according to the claimant's claim, thus including mistaken views. The commentator further clarifies terms like 'balkafa' and discusses the possibility that 'taken from the Book' means adherence to legal principles. He concludes that if the condition is understood as truth in reality, it fails to exclude divine philosophy, whose proponents also claim truth.

Key Terms
قانون الإسلام
المسائل الحقة
المخطئ
المجسمة
المعتزلة
البلكفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The criterion of Islamic law cleanly separates true kalam from false doctrines.
Correction: This objection shows that even false sects claim their views are Islamic, so the criterion must include claims, not just objective truth.

Checkpoint
What does the second objection primarily demonstrate?
A) The law of Islam excludes all false doctrines from kalam.
B) Mistaken theologians are not part of kalam.
C) The criterion fails because both true and false claimants invoke Islamic law.
D) The Mujassima are not kalam.

Key Takeaway
The second objection reveals that the Islamic law criterion is too narrow because it would exclude the very practitioners of kalam who are in error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter someone whose beliefs differ from yours, do you ever dismiss them as not being 'real' Muslims or scholars? What does this passage teach you about the inclusion of even mistaken theologians in the field of kalam, and how might that change your attitude towards those you disagree with?
?
Are you quick to judge others' theology as outside the fold of Islam? How does the author's mention of the Mujassima and Mu'tazila as part of kalam challenge your instinct to exclude, and what criteria do you actually use to decide who is a true Muslim?
?
The law of Islam criterion seemed sound but failed upon scrutiny. Think of a personal 'criterion' you use to evaluate others' faith—perhaps based on actions, knowledge, or affiliation. Could that criterion also be flawed? What would it take for you to recognize that your standard might be too narrow?

Answer to the Objection: Broadening the Criterion to Include Claims
Al-Sharh provides the answer to the second objection and discusses key terms and a remaining problem.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the commentator answers the second objection by reinterpreting 'law of Islam' to include the claimant's perspective.

Core Idea
The objection is solved by saying 'law of Islam' means what the claimant believes to be true, not only objective truth.

Having presented the objection, the commentator now offers an answer. He argues that the intended meaning of 'research according to Islamic law' is that the issues are taken from the Book and follow legal principles. Moreover, the law of Islam is understood as what is true according to the claimant's claim, thus including mistaken views. This response preserves the inclusion of heretical theologians while maintaining a link to Islamic sources.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer and note the key reinterpretation
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the answer: 'the law of Islam is that which is true, even if by the claimant's claim'. Understand how this broadens the criterion.
This reinterpretation allows mistaken theologians to remain within the definition.
2
Understand the term 'balkafa' and its context
The commentator explains 'balkafa' as derived from 'bila kayfiyya' (without modality). This clarifies a type of theologian who avoids anthropomorphism by negating modality.
This shows the commentator's attention to precise terminology.
3
Consider the concluding nuance about divine philosophy
At the end, the commentator points out that if 'truth' is generalized to both actual and claimed truth, the definition still fails to exclude divine philosophy, whose proponents also claim truth.
This suggests the answer is not fully satisfactory and further refinement is needed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

What Is Kalam?
intermediate

Objection and answer regarding the condition of the Law of Islam
Defense of the definition of kalam against the objection of excluding mistaken schools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the commentator defends the definition of kalam against the objection that the condition 'according to the Law of Islam' mistakenly excludes mistaken schools.

Core Idea
The condition of Islam includes even mistaken views because it judges by the claimant's belief.

The definition of kalam includes the phrase 'according to the Law of Islam' to distinguish it from philosophy. But an objection arises: doesn't this exclude erroneous schools from kalam? The commentator argues that it actually includes them, because the Law of Islam considers truth even in the claimant's belief. This passage shows how precise theological definitions handle objections.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the first part where the objection is raised that the condition excludes mistaken schools, and the answer that the Law of Islam includes them by intent.
Notice the phrase 'ولو بزعم الزاعم' — this is key.
2
Understand the gloss on 'al-balkafah'
The commentator explains the term 'البلكفة' meaning 'bila kayfiyyah' (without modality). This is a reference to a school that avoids anthropomorphism by negating modality.
This gloss clarifies a technical term used in the definition.
3
Analyze the note on 'taken from the Book'
The commentator explains that 'taken from the Book' means preserving legal principles and not contradicting certainties in one's belief. This affects the ruling of takfir.
Consider how this connects to the broader issue of defining kalam.
4
Review the final objection and answer
Read the final objection that if 'right' is general, then divine philosophy is not excluded. The answer specifies that 'right' here means what is in accordance with Islam.
This reinforces the distinctiveness of the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (الثاني قانون إلخ حاصله أن هذا القيد وإن أفاد امتيازه عن الإلهي، لكنه مخل بالتعريف لأن قانون الإسلام إنما هو المسائل الحقة، فيلزم خروج مسائل المخطئ عن الكلام، وهو خلاف المقرر عندهم، وإن التزم مخالفة القوم يلزم عدم امتيازه عما ليس بكلام أعني مسائل المخطئ لأنه أيضاً يدعي أنها حقة، والجواب أن قانون الإسلام ما هو الحق، ولو بزعم الزاعم فيشمل مسائل المخطئ.
قوله : (بالبلكفة) مأخوذ من بلا كيفية أي المستترين بنفي الكيفية حيث يقولون : أنه تعالى مستو على العرش لا كاستوائنا له وله وجه ويد لا كوجهنا ويدنا، وفي بعض النسخ بالكيفية فالباء للتعدية أي السائرين للكيفية.
قوله : ( مأخوذة من الكتاب لعل مراده بالأخذ أن يحافظ في جميع تلك المباحث على القواعد الشرعية، ولا يخالف القطعية منها في اعتقاده فلا يرد أنه إذا لم يكن المخطئ مخالفاً للمسائل القطعية لا يصح تكفيره لأن من يكفره يعتقد أنه مخالف للقطعية، وإن لم يكن
قوله : (مع أن هذا الزعم منه (باطل لا يقال : المراد بالحق أعم مما في نفس الأمر وعند الزاعم لأنا نقول : إذا أريد بقانون الإسلام ما هو الحق، وعمم الحق لكلا القسمين لم يحصل المطلوب وهو خروج الإلهي لأن صاحبه أيضاً يدعي حقيته.
His statement: (Second: the Law of Islam, etc.) Its summary: This condition, although it distinguishes it from the Divine Science, nevertheless it spoils the definition, because the Law of Islam is only the true issues. Thus it follows that the issues of the mistaken one are excluded from kalam, which is contrary to what is established among them. And if one insists on contradicting the people, then it follows that it is not distinguished from what is not kalam, i.e., the issues of the mistaken one, because he also claims they are true. And the answer is that the Law of Islam is what is true, even if by the claimant's belief, so it includes the issues of the mistaken one. His statement: (By al-Balkafah) It is derived from 'bila kayfiyyah' (without modality), meaning those who conceal themselves by negating modality, saying: He is established above the Throne not like our establishment, and He has a face and a hand not like our face and hand. In some copies it is 'bil-kayfiyyah', so the ba' is for transitivity, meaning those who follow modality. His statement: (Taken from the Book) Perhaps his intention by 'taking' is that he preserves in all those investigations the legal principles, and he does not contradict the certain ones among them in his belief. So it cannot be objected that if the mistaken one is not contradicting the certain issues, his takfir is invalid, because the one who declares him a disbeliever believes that he is contradicting certainties, even if he is not. His statement: (And this claim of his is false) It cannot be said: The intended meaning of 'right' is more general, including what is true in itself and what is true in the claimant's opinion. For we say: If by 'Law of Islam' is meant what is right, and 'right' is generalized to both categories, the desired result is not achieved, which is the exclusion of the Divine Science, because its practitioner also claims its truth.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a series of objections and answers defending the definition of kalam. The author's text included the condition 'according to the Law of Islam' to distinguish kalam from divine philosophy. The commentator presents an objection: this condition spoils the definition because it restricts kalam to true issues, thus excluding the issues of mistaken scholars (e.g., anthropomorphists) who are still considered part of kalam. The answer is that 'the Law of Islam' means 'what is true' even if only in the claimant's belief, so it includes mistaken views. The commentator then glosses the term 'al-balkafah' (bila kayfiyyah) used for those who avoid anthropomorphism by denying modality. Next, a note on 'taken from the Book' explains that the condition means preserving legal principles and not contradicting certainties in one's belief, so that the takfir of a mistaken scholar depends on the belief of the one declaring takfir. Finally, another objection: if 'right' is general, then divine philosophers also claim truth, so the distinction is lost. The answer is that the definition intends 'right' in the specific sense of what is in accordance with Islam, not general truth.

Key Terms
قانون الإسلام
مسائل المخطئ
البلكفة
القطعية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The condition 'according to the Law of Islam' in the definition of kalam excludes all mistaken or heretical schools from the discipline.
Correction: The commentator explains that the condition includes mistaken schools because 'the Law of Islam' means what is true even by the claimant's belief, so their views are still considered kalam.

Checkpoint
How does the commentator answer the objection that the condition 'قانون الإسلام' excludes the issues of the mistaken scholar from kalam?
A) By stating that the Law of Islam is only the true issues, so mistaken views are excluded.
B) By stating that the Law of Islam means what is true, even if only by the claimant's belief, so it includes mistaken views.
C) By arguing that the mistaken scholar is not actually a practitioner of kalam.
D) By redefining the Law of Islam to include only what is agreed upon.

Key Takeaway
The condition 'Law of Islam' in the definition of kalam is interpreted broadly to include mistaken schools, preserving the inclusivity of the discipline.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you meet someone whose religious views differ from yours, do you instinctively label them as 'mistaken' and exclude them? How does this lesson's inclusive interpretation of 'the Law of Islam' challenge you to reconsider your judgment of others' intentions?
?
Have you ever confidently declared a fellow Muslim's belief as invalid (like takfir) based on your own understanding of certainties? How does the commentator's allowance for 'claimant's belief' hold you accountable for being more cautious in such declarations?
?
In your personal study of aqeedah, have you dismissed a scholar's view because you assumed it contradicted Islamic principles? What practical steps can you take to apply the principle of 'preserving legal principles' while remaining open to different interpretations, as the passage suggests?

Clarifying the Condition of Not Contradicting Certainties
The commentator resolves the issue of contradictory certainties by distinguishing types of opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the condition of not contradicting certainties in kalam applies only to contradiction by mere desire, not to contradiction based on following another textual evidence.

Core Idea
Contradicting certainties by following another text is not a violation of kalam's condition.

The commentator addresses a potential objection: if kalam requires not contradicting certainties, how can we consider groups like the Mujassimah as kalam scholars? He resolves this by distinguishing two types of contradiction. This lesson unpacks that crucial distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument unfold.
Notice the structure: condition, problem, two possibilities, resolution.
2
Identify the problem
The problem is about the Mujassimah: if their doctrine contradicts certainty, they are not kalam scholars; if not, we cannot declare them disbelievers. Why is this a dilemma?
The dilemma hinges on the definition of kalam requiring no contradiction of certainties.
3
Understand the distinction
The commentator differentiates two ways of contradicting certainties: by mere desire of the soul, and by following another text. Only the first is negated in the definition.
The phrase 'جرياً على مقتضى نظر العقول القاصرة' hints at following a deficient intellectual requirement.
4
Connect to the bigger picture
This refinement ensures that kalam remains open to different interpretations based on textual evidence, not arbitrary desires.
It preserves the integrity of kalam as a rational discipline grounded in revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ما ينسب إليهما من الإجماع والمعقول الذي لا يخالفهما، وبالجملة فحاصله : أن يحافظ في جميع المباحث على القواعد الشرعية، ولا يخالف القطعيات منها جرياً على ما هو مقتضى نظر العقول القاصرة على ما هو قانون الفلسفة كذا في شرح المقاصد، وفيه بحث وهو أن بعض أرباب الكلام نكفره كالمجسمة، فإن لم يكن مذهبهم مخالفاً للقطع لزم أن لا نكفرهم، وإن كان مخالفاً له لزم أن لا يكون من أرباب الكلام اللهم إلا أن يقال المراد من مخالفة القطعيات المنفية المخالفة بمجرد هوى النفس وأما مخالفة القطع إتباعاً لمشابهة نص آخر فليس من المخالفة المنفية ها هنا كما يشهد به قوله جرياً على مقتضى نظر العقول القاصرة.
His statement: (And what is attributed to them of consensus and the intellect that does not contradict them. In summary, its gist is: that he preserves in all investigations the legal principles, and does not contradict the certain ones among them, proceeding according to the requirement of the deficient intellects in the manner of the law of philosophy, as in Sharh al-Maqasid. And in it there is a discussion: that some of the people of kalam we declare them disbelievers, like the Mujassimah. If their doctrine is not contradictory to certainty, then it follows that we do not declare them disbelievers. And if it is contradictory to it, then it follows that they are not from the people of kalam. Unless it is said: The intended meaning of the negated contradiction of certainties is contradiction merely by the desire of the soul. As for contradicting certainty by following the resemblance of another text, that is not from the negated contradiction here, as is witnessed by his statement: 'proceeding according to the requirement of the deficient intellects'.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage addresses a further objection about the condition of not contradicting certainties. It clarifies that the intention is to preserve legal principles and avoid contradicting certainties, but following the requirement of deficient intellects as in philosophy. Then it raises a problem: we declare some kalam scholars like the Mujassimah as disbelievers. If their views are not against certainty, then takfir is invalid; if they are against certainty, then they are not kalam scholars. The answer distinguishes contradictory by mere desire from contradictory by following another text, noting that the latter is not negated here. The commentary thus refines the condition to allow for differing interpretations based on textual evidence.

القطعيات
المجسمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any contradiction of certainties excludes one from kalam.
Correction: The commentator shows that contradicting certainty by following another text is acceptable and does not exclude one from kalam.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what type of contradiction of certainties is not negated in the definition of kalam?
A) Contradiction by mere desire of the soul.
B) Contradiction by following the resemblance of another text.
C) Contradiction by ignorance.
D) Contradiction by denial of revelation.

Key Takeaway
In kalam, contradicting certainties by following another text is not a violation of the condition, only contradiction by mere desire is.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Qur'an or hadith, how often do you stop to ask whether your understanding is driven by your own desires or by a sincere attempt to follow the text as it is? Can you recall a time when you twisted a verse to justify something you wanted?
?
This lesson shows that even a valid interpretation can contradict a certainty if it follows another text. Are there beliefs you hold that you have never questioned, thinking they are certain, but which might actually be based on personal preference? Are you willing to examine them?
?
The Mujassimah were declared disbelievers for their literal reading. In your heart, do you fear that some of your own deeply held views might be similarly misguided? Will you commit to learning the principles of correct interpretation so you do not fall into error?

What Is Kalam?

Why Study Ilm al-Kalam? Its Four Essential Benefits
The author enumerates the first four benefits of ilm al-kalam and explains their significance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four key benefits of studying ilm al-kalam: personal elevation from imitation to certainty, guiding and compelling others, preserving the religion, and serving as the foundation for all other religious sciences.

Core Idea
Ilm al-Kalam provides the foundation for all Islamic sciences and elevates the believer from imitation to certainty.

Why should we study ilm al-kalam? This passage from the Muqaddimat explains that every science is pursued for its benefit. The author then lists four benefits of kalam, showing that it is not merely a speculative discipline but has practical, social, and foundational purposes. Let's explore these benefits one by one.

Guided Path
1
Understand the role of benefit
Notice that the passage begins by stating that studying a science requires knowing its benefit, otherwise it is conventionally futile. This sets the stage for the list of benefits.
The author distinguishes conventional futility from linguistic futility—kalam has real benefit.
2
First benefit: Personal ascent
The first benefit is for the individual: rising from blind imitation (taqlid) to firm certainty (yaqin). The Quranic verse 58:11 is cited to emphasize the high rank of scholars of certainty.
This benefit addresses the student's own intellectual and spiritual development.
3
Second benefit: Guiding and compelling others
The second benefit is social: guiding those who seek the truth and compelling the obstinate by establishing clear proofs. This may even lead the obstinate to submit.
This shows kalam's role in da'wah and debate.
4
Third benefit: Preserving the religion
The third benefit is protective: kalam safeguards the foundational rules (qawa'id) of Islam from the doubts of falsifiers.
This is a defensive function against attacks on the faith.
5
Fourth benefit: Foundation of religious sciences
The fourth benefit is foundational: all other religious sciences (tafsir, hadith, fiqh, usul) depend on kalam to establish the existence of God, prophethood, etc. Without kalam, they lack a basis.
This highlights kalam as the mother science (umm al-'ulum).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الموقف الأول في المقدمات - المقصد الثالث : فائدته
عبثًا عرفاً ( وليزداد ) عطف على دفعاً ( رغبةً فيه إذا كان ( ذلك العلم ( مهماً ) للطالب بسبب فائدته التي عرفها فيوفيه حقه من الجد والاجتهاد في تحصيله بحسب تلك الفائدة ( وهي ( أي فائدة علم الكلام ( أمور (الأول) بالنظر إلى الشخص في قوته النظرية وهو ( الترقي من حضيض التقليد إلى ذروة الإيقان ويرفع الله الذين آمنوا منكم والذين أوتوا العلم درجات ﴾ [المجادلة : (۱۱] خص العلماء الموقنين بالذكر مع اندراجهم في المؤمنين رفعاً لمنزلتهم كأنه قال : وخصوصاً هؤلاء الأعلام منكم ( الثاني ) بالنظر إلى تكميل الغير وهو ( إرشاد المسترشدين بإيضاح المحجة) لهم إلى عقائد الدين ) وإلزام المعاندين بإقامة الحجة ( عليهم فإن هذا الإلزام المشتمل على تفضيح المعاند ربما جره إلى الإذعان والاسترشاد، فيكون نافعاً له ومكملاً إياه ( الثالث ) بالنسبة إلى أصول الإسلام وهو ( حفظ قواعد الدين) وهي تزلزلها شبه المبطلين الرابع بالنظر إلى فروعه وهو ( أن يبني عليه العلوم الشرعية ) أي يبني عليه ما عداه منها ( فإنه أساسها وإليه يؤول أخذها واقتباسها ) فإنه ما لم يثبت وجود صانع عالم قادر مكلف مرسل للرسل منزل للكتب، لم يتصور علم تفسير وحديث ولا علم فقه وأصوله، فكلها متوقفة على علم الكلام مقتبسة منه، فالآخذ فيها بدونه كبان على غير أساس وإذا سئل عما هو فيه لم يقدر على برهان ولا قياس بخلاف المستنبطين لها فإنهم كانوا عالمين بحقيقته، وإن لم تكن فيما بينهم هذه الاصطلاحات المستحدثة فيما بيننا كما في علم الفقه بعينه ( الخامس ) بالنظر
قوله : ( عبثاً عرفاً) فإن العبث العرفي ما لا يترتب عليه فائدة معتد بها في نظره وفيه إشارة إلى أن المراد بقوله : دفعاً للعبث العرفي لا اللغوي وهو ما لا يترتب عليه فائدة أصلاً، فإنه ممتنع في تحصيل العلوم.
قوله : ( عطف على دفعاً بحسب المعنى أي طلباً للازدياد وإنما صرح باللام فيه لعدم كونه فعلا لفاعل الفعل المعلل به.
قوله : ( ويرفع الله الذين إلخ الواو من الحكاية والكلام من قبيل الالتفات بمعنى تعقيب الكلام بجملة مستقلة ملاقية له في المعنى على طريق التمثيل أو الدعاء أو نحوهما نحو قولهم قصم الفقر ظهري، والفقر من قاصمات الظهر والتلاقي بينهما ظاهر فإن تخصيص العلماء بعد دخولهم في الذين آمنوا يدل على رفعة شأنهم لأجل العلم .
يكون للفاعل أغراض مختلفة من أفعال مختلفة، وتكون الفائدة التي اعتقد فيه موافقة لغرضه من فعل آخر، وإن لم تكن موافقة لغرضه من ذلك الفعل، فليتأمل .
The First Station in the Preliminaries - The Third Purpose: Its Benefit
It is conventionally futile (abathan ‘urfan) – and [the phrase] 'and in order to increase' is coordinated with 'to repel' (daf‘an) in meaning, i.e., seeking increase; (desire for it) if that science is important to the student due to its benefit which he has come to know, then he gives it its due of seriousness and effort in acquiring it according to that benefit. And they (i.e., the benefits of ilm al-kalam) are matters:
First, with regard to the person in his theoretical faculty: it is the ascent from the lowland of imitation (taqlid) to the summit of certainty (yaqin). And Allah raises those who have believed among you and those who have been given knowledge by degrees [al-Mujadilah: 11]. He specified the scholars who are certain along with their inclusion among the believers to elevate their rank, as if He said: 'and especially these distinguished ones among you.'
Second, with regard to completing others: it is guiding the seekers by clarifying the path for them to the creeds of the religion, and compelling the obstinate by establishing the proof against them. For this compulsion, which includes exposing the obstinate, may perhaps drag him to submission and seeking guidance, thus beneficial for him and completing him.
Third, with regard to the foundations of Islam: it is preserving the rules of the religion, which are shaken by the doubts of the falsifiers.
Fourth, with regard to its branches: it is that the religious sciences are built upon it, i.e., all other religious sciences are built upon it, for it is their foundation and to it their derivation and adoption go back. For as long as the existence of a Maker, Knowing, Capable, Imposing obligations, Sending messengers, Revealing books is not established, no science of tafsir, hadith, fiqh, or usul al-fiqh can be conceived. Thus, all of them depend on ilm al-kalam and are derived from it. So one who engages in them without it is like a builder without a foundation, and when asked about what he is doing, he cannot provide proof or analogy, unlike those who derive them, for they were knowledgeable of its reality, even if these recently invented terminologies among us were not among them, as in the case of fiqh itself.
Fifth, with regard to...
His saying: 'conventionally futile' – for conventional futility is that which does not yield a benefit considered significant in his view. And in it there is an indication that what is meant by his saying 'to repel conventional futility' is not linguistic futility, which is that which does not yield any benefit at all, for that is impossible in the acquisition of sciences.
His saying: 'coordinated with daf‘an in meaning' – i.e., seeking increase, and he explicitly put the lam (for) because it is not an action of the agent of the act that is being given a reason.
His saying: 'and Allah raises those who have been given knowledge' – the waw (and) is from the narrative, and the speech is of the type of iltifat (turning), meaning the continuation of speech with an independent sentence that meets it in meaning, by way of exemplification or supplication or the like, such as their saying: 'Poverty broke my back, and poverty is one of the breakers of backs.' The correspondence between them is apparent, for specifying the scholars after their inclusion in 'those who have believed' indicates the elevation of their status because of knowledge.
The agent may have different purposes from different actions, and the benefit that he believed in may be in accordance with his purpose from another action, even if it is not in accordance with his purpose from that action, so reflect.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the benefits of ilm al-kalam. It first clarifies that engaging in a science requires knowing its benefit and that the phrase 'conventionally futile' indicates the repulsion of conventional futility (insignificant benefit) not linguistic futility (no benefit at all). Then four benefits are listed: (1) Personal: elevation from taqlid to yaqin, supported by Quran 58:11 which singles out scholars of certainty. (2) Social: guiding seekers and compelling obstinate opponents, which may lead to their submission. (3) Protective: preserving the foundational rules of religion against doubts. (4) Foundational: all other religious sciences (tafsir, hadith, fiqh, usul) depend on kalam for their premises; without proving God, prophethood, etc., these sciences have no basis. The fifth benefit is cut off. Additional commentary explains the grammatical structure of the Quranic verse (iltifat) and concludes with a reflection on how an agent's different purposes may align with benefits from different actions.

Correction: The passage shows four distinct benefits: personal, social (guiding and compelling), protective (preserving the religion), and foundational (basis for all other religious sciences).

The Five Benefits of Ilm al-Kalam
Jurjani enumerates the five benefits of ilm al-kalam and explains each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five benefits of ilm al-kalam as enumerated by al-Jurjani, which demonstrate its theoretical, practical, and social importance.

Core Idea
Ilm al-kalam is not just theory—it elevates certainty, guides others, protects Islam, supports all religious sciences, and leads to bliss.

Before delving into the detailed arguments of kalam, Jurjani motivates the student by explaining why this science is worth studying. He enumerates five benefits that cover personal growth, teaching others, defending Islam, providing a foundation for all Islamic sciences, and achieving salvation. This passage sets the stage for the entire study.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its structure and key terms. Then read the translation carefully.
Notice that the passage begins with a general remark about benefit before listing the five items.
2
Identify the Five Benefits
The passage lists five benefits of ilm al-kalam. Locate each one and note the perspective from which each is described (e.g., theoretical, social, foundational).
The benefits are introduced with ordinal numbers (الأول, الثاني, etc.).
3
Reflect on the Qur'anic Verse
The author quotes Quran 58:11 to support the first benefit. Consider how this verse emphasizes the elevated rank of scholars with certainty.
This shows that the first benefit is rooted in scriptural evidence.
4
Understand the Foundational Role
The fourth benefit explains how kalam underlies all other religious sciences. Reflect on why tafsir, hadith, and fiqh depend on kalam.
The author uses the analogy of a builder without a foundation.
5
Connect to the Ultimate Goal
The fifth benefit culminates in the bliss of both worlds. Consider how all the previous benefits contribute to this ultimate end.
The author states that this bliss is desired for itself and is the final goal.

الموقف الأول في المقدمات - المقصد الثالث : فائدته عبثاً عرفاً وليزداد عطف على دفعاً رغبةً فيه إذا كان ذلك العلم مهماً للطالب بسبب فائدته التي عرفها فيوفيه حقه من الجد والاجتهاد في تحصيله بحسب تلك الفائدة وهي أي فائدة علم الكلام أمور الأول بالنظر إلى الشخص في قوته النظرية وهو الترقي من حضيض التقليد إلى ذروة الإيقان ويرفع الله الذين آمنوا منكم والذين أوتوا العلم درجات [المجادلة:11] خص العلماء الموقنين بالذكر مع اندراجهم في المؤمنين رفعاً لمنزلتهم كأنه قال وخصوصاً هؤلاء الأعلام منكم الثاني بالنظر إلى تكميل الغير وهو إرشاد المسترشدين بإيضاح المحجة لهم إلى عقائد الدين وإلزام المعاندين بإقامة الحجة عليهم فإن هذا الإلزام المشتمل على تفضيح المعاند ربما جره إلى الإذعان والاسترشاد فيكون نافعاً له ومكملاً إياه الثالث بالنسبة إلى أصول الإسلام وهو حفظ قواعد الدين وهي تزلزلها شبه المبطلين الرابع بالنظر إلى فروعه وهو أن يبني عليه العلوم الشرعية أي يبني عليه ما عداه منها فإنه أساسها وإليه يؤول أخذها واقتباسها فإنه ما لم يثبت وجود صانع عالم قادر مكلف مرسل للرسل منزل للكتب لم يتصور علم تفسير وحديث ولا علم فقه وأصوله فكلها متوقفة على علم الكلام مقتبسة منه فالآخذ فيها بدونه كبان على غير أساس وإذا سئل عما هو فيه لم يقدر على برهان ولا قياس بخلاف المستنبطين لها فإنهم كانوا عالمين بحقيقته وإن لم تكن فيما بينهم هذه الاصطلاحات المستحدثة فيما بيننا كما في علم الفقه بعينه الخامس بالنظر إلى الشخص في قوته العملية وهو صحة النية بإخلاصهم في الأعمال وصحة الاعتقاد بقوته في الأحكام المتعلقة بالأفعال إذ بها أي بهذه الصحة في النية والاعتقاد يرجى قبول العمل وترتب الثواب عليه وغاية ذلك كله أي والفائدة التي يفيدها ما ذكر من الأمور الخمسة وتنتهي إليها هي الفوز بسعادة الدارين فإن هذا الفوز مطلوب لذاته فهو منتهى الأغراض وغاية الغايات
The First Stand - Introductions - Third Purpose: Its Benefit. [It is] conventionally futile (عبثاً عرفاً) and [the phrase] 'and that he may increase' (ليزداد) is coordinated with 'to repel' (دفعاً) in meaning, [meaning] desiring increase in it when that knowledge is important for the student due to its benefit which he knows, so he gives it its due of earnestness and effort in acquiring it according to that benefit. And it (i.e., the benefit of the science of kalam) is matters: First, with respect to the person in his theoretical power: it is ascent from the lowland of blind following to the summit of certainty, and 'Allah will raise those who have believed among you and those who have been given knowledge, by degrees' (Qur'an 58:11). He specified the certain scholars with mention while they are included among the believers, raising their station, as if He said: and especially these eminent ones among you. Second, with respect to perfecting others: it is guiding the seekers by clarifying the path for them to the beliefs of the religion, and compelling the obstinate by establishing the proof against them, for this compulsion which includes disgracing the obstinate may draw him to submission and seeking guidance, thus it is beneficial for him and perfects him. Third, with respect to the foundations of Islam: it is preserving the rules of religion from being shaken by the doubts of the falsifiers. Fourth, with respect to its branches: it is that the religious sciences are built upon it, i.e., what is other than them from it, for it is their foundation and to it returns their derivation and borrowing. For as long as the existence of a Maker, Knowing, Powerful, Obligator, Sender of messengers, Revelator of books is not established, the science of exegesis, hadith, jurisprudence and its principles cannot be conceived. So all of them depend on the science of kalam and are borrowed from it. Thus the one who engages in them without it is like a builder without a foundation, and if asked about what he is in, he cannot produce a proof or analogy, unlike those who derive them, for they were knowers of its reality, even if these recently invented terminologies among us did not exist among them, just as in the science of jurisprudence itself. Fifth, with respect to the person in his practical power: it is the soundness of intention by sincerity in deeds, and the soundness of belief by his power in the rulings related to actions. For by it (i.e., this soundness in intention and belief) acceptance of the deed and the consequent reward is hoped for. And the ultimate end of all that (i.e., the benefit that the mentioned five matters yield and to which they lead) is victory in the bliss of the two abodes. For this victory is desired for itself, so it is the ultimate of goals and the final end of ends.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the five benefits (fawa'id) of ilm al-kalam. The author begins by stating that the benefit is what motivates the student to earnest effort. He then lists the benefits: (1) Theoretical perfection: the student ascends from taqlid to yaqin, with a Qur'anic verse emphasizing the elevated rank of scholars. (2) Perfecting others: guiding seekers and compelling the obstinate with proofs. (3) Preserving Islam's foundations from doubts. (4) Supporting the religious sciences: kalam is the basis for tafsir, hadith, fiqh, etc.; without it these sciences lack foundation. (5) Practical benefits: sincerity in intention and soundness of belief, leading to acceptance of deeds and ultimately to the bliss of both worlds. The passage proceeds in the author's order, explaining each benefit in sequence.

The Rank of Ilm al-Kalam
Jurjani explains the rank and honor of ilm al-kalam based on its subject matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why knowing the rank of a science is important and how the subject matter of ilm al-kalam makes it the most honored science.

Core Idea
The honor of a science comes from the nobility of its subject matter.

Before diving into the study of any science, it is essential to appreciate its value and standing among other disciplines. This lesson introduces the concept of the rank (martaba) of ilm al-kalam, explaining why it is considered the most honored science. By understanding its subject matter — the most general and highest of things — we recognize why this science deserves our utmost dedication.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Notice the flow from the necessity of presenting rank to the description of the subject.
2
Identify why rank must be presented
Find the phrase that states why the rank of a science should be known before studying it. What purpose does this knowledge serve?
The author says it is to know its value and to give it proper effort.
3
Examine the subject of kalam
Look at how the author describes the subject matter of kalam. What two characteristics does it have?
The subject is the most general (a'amm) and the highest (a'la) of things.
4
Reflect on why this makes kalam honored
Consider why a science with the most general and highest subject matter is considered the most honored. What does it include?
It includes the investigations of Allah's essence, attributes, and actions.

Source Text

المقصد الرابع : مرتبته أي شرفه، وإنما وجب تقديم مرتبة العلم الذي يطلب أن يشرع فيه ليعرف قدره ورتبته فيما بين العلوم فيوفى حقه من الجد والاعتناء في اكتسابه واقتنائه، إذا عرفت هذا فنقول قد علمت أن موضوعه أي موضوع الكلام وهو المعلوم أعم الأمور وأعلاها فيتناول أشرف المعلومات التي هي مباحث ذاته تعالى وصفاته وأفعاله
The Fourth Purpose: Its Rank, i.e., its honor. And it was necessary to present the rank of the science which one seeks to begin in order to know its value and rank among the sciences, so that it may be given its due of earnestness and care in its acquisition and possession. If you know this, then we say: You have known that its subject (i.e., the subject of kalam, which is the known) is the most general and highest of things, so it includes the most honorable of known things, which are the investigations of His essence, may He be exalted, His attributes, and His actions.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the rank (martaba) or honor (sharaf) of ilm al-kalam. The author states that knowing the rank of a science is necessary before studying it, so that the student gives it proper effort. He then explains that the subject matter of kalam is the most general and highest (a'amm al-umur wa a'laha), and therefore it includes the most honorable objects of knowledge: the essence of God, His attributes, and His actions. The passage argues that because the subject is the highest, the science itself is honored. The author follows the logical order: why rank is presented, what the subject is, and why that makes the science noble.

The Rank and Subject Matter of Kalam
Defining the rank of kalam and its subject matter as the most general.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Kalam's nobility comes from its subject: the most general and highest reality, Allah.

Before diving into the content of kalam, the author explains why it deserves serious study. The rank of a science reflects its status, and kalam deals with the highest possible subject: the essence, attributes, and actions of Allah. This passage establishes that kalam is the noblest science because its subject is the noblest.

Four Objections to Kalam's Subject Matter Claim
Enumeration of four objections to the subject matter claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four objections raised against the claim that the subject matter of kalam is the noblest known things.

Core Idea
Honor through subject generality is redundant without investigative mode.

Before delving into the response, we must examine the objections that challenge the logical structure of the claim about kalam's subject matter. These objections question the need for additional statements, the nature of investigations vs. problems, and the focus of honor. Understanding these objections is crucial for appreciating the nuance of the resolution.

Guided Path
1
Read the four objections
Read the Arabic passage listing the four objections. Notice how each one challenges a different aspect of the previous claim.
2
Identify the logical flaws
For each objection, identify what logical flaw it points to: redundancy, confusion of subject and problems, misplacement of honor, or wrong perspective.
The objections are numbered: first, second, third, fourth.
3
Consider the underlying assumptions
Think about why these objections arise. What implicit assumptions about science hierarchy, subject-problem relation, and honor attribution are at play?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فيتناول) إلخ فيه اختلال من وجوه أما أولاً فلأنه لا حاجة إلى هذا التفريع بعد التصريح بأن موضوعه أعم الأمور أي الموضوعات لما تقرر أن العلوم تتصاعد بتصاعد الموضوعات عموماً وخصوصاً، وأما ثانياً فلان مباحث ذاته تعالى وصفاته وأفعاله من المسائل ولا معنى لتناول الموضوع للمسائل، وأما ثالثاً فلان على صحته يفيد إثبات شرافة الموضوع وأما رابعاً فلان قوله لا شك إنه إذا كان المعلوم إلخ يفيد إثبات شرافة العلم باعتبار معلومه والمقصود إثبات شرافته باعتبار موضوعه وغاية التوجيه أنه قدس سره حمل الأعلى على معنى الأشرف، لا على الأعلى رتبة ليكون تأسيساً، والفاء في قوله فيتناول تعليلية أو استئنافية أو زائدة والجملة تعليل لكونه أشرف الموضوعات، والضمير المستتر راجع إلى موضوعه وقيد الحيثية ملحوظ أي لأنه يتناول موضوعه من حيث أنه موضوع أي مبحوث عنه في العلم أشرف المعلومات التي هي ذاته تعالى وصفاته وأفعاله من حيث كونها مبحوثاً عنها ولم يكتف بتناوله للأمور الثلاثة من حيث أنفسها لأنه لا يفيد شرافة العلم، ألا ترى أن موضوع النحو يتناول كلامه تعالى وكلام الرسول، ولا يلزم منه أشرفيته من علم التفسير والحديث، وللإشارة إلى كون التناول من حيث البحث محط الشرافة قدم لفظ المباحث، فالحاصل أن موضوع الكلام أعم الموضوعات فيكون أشرف لأن العلوم تتصاعد بتصاعد الموضوعات، وأن موضوعه أشرف الموضوعات لتناوله ذاته وصفاته وأفعاله التي هي أشرف المعلومات، ولا شك أن المعلوم الذي هو الموضوع إذا كان أشرف بسبب ذلك التناول كان العلم المتعلق به أي الباحث عن أحواله أشرف وخلاصته إثبات شرافة موضوعه باعتبار شموله للموضوعات، وباعتباره في نفسه ولذا عبر عن الموضوع في قوله ولا شك إلخ بالمعلوم.
His saying: 'so it encompasses' etc. There is in it a disorder from several aspects. First: there is no need for this branching after the explicit statement that its subject is the most general of matters, i.e., of subjects, because it is established that sciences ascend with the ascending of subjects in generality and specificity. Second: the investigations of His essence, attributes, and actions are from among the problems, and there is no meaning to the subject encompassing the problems. Third: if it is correct, it would prove the honor of the subject. Fourth: his saying 'there is no doubt that when the known is nobler' etc. proves the honor of the science in consideration of its known object, but the intention is to prove its honor in consideration of its subject. The ultimate interpretation is that he, may God sanctify his secret, interpreted 'higher' in the sense of 'nobler', not in the sense of 'higher in rank', so that it would be an original point. The 'fa' in his saying 'so it encompasses' is explanatory, or resumptive, or redundant, and the sentence is an explanation of its being the noblest of subjects. The implicit pronoun refers to its subject, and the restriction of 'from where it is a subject' is taken into account, i.e., because it encompasses its subject from the perspective that it is a subject, i.e., investigated in the science, the noblest of known things, which are His essence, attributes, and actions from the aspect that they are investigated. He did not content himself with its encompassing the three things from the aspect of themselves because that would not entail the honor of the science. Do you not see that the subject of grammar encompasses the speech of God and the speech of the Messenger, yet it does not follow that it is nobler than the science of exegesis and hadith? And to indicate that the encompassing from the perspective of investigation is the locus of honor, he introduced the word 'investigations'. The upshot is that the subject of kalam is the most general of subjects, so it is nobler because sciences ascend with the ascending of subjects, and its subject is the noblest of subjects because it encompasses His essence, attributes, and actions which are the noblest of known things. There is no doubt that when the known which is the subject is nobler due to that encompassing, the science related to it — i.e., that which investigates its states — is nobler. The summary is the proof of the honor of its subject in consideration of its including subjects, and in consideration of itself. For that reason he expressed the subject in his saying 'there is no doubt' etc. as 'the known'.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. It begins by presenting four objections to the earlier claim that the subject matter of kalam encompasses the noblest known things (God's essence, attributes, actions) and thereby demonstrates the science's honor. The first objection: since it was already stated that the subject is the most general of matters, the additional statement that it is the highest (أعلاها) is redundant — generality already implies superiority. Second: the investigations (مباحث) of God's essence, etc. are actually the problems (مسائل) of the science, not part of the subject; a subject does not encompass its own problems. Third: even if it did encompass them, it would only prove the honor of the subject, not of the science itself. Fourth: the later statement 'when the known is nobler, the science is nobler' proves honor from the perspective of the known object (المعلوم), but the goal here is to prove honor from the perspective of the subject (موضوع). The answer resolves each point. The author explains that the word 'highest' (أعلاها) is interpreted as 'noblest' (أشرف), not 'higher in rank' (أعلى رتبة), to make an original point. The 'fa' in 'فيتناول' can be explanatory or resumptive, and the entire clause is an explanation that the subject is the noblest of subjects. The implicit pronoun in 'يتناول' refers to the subject, and the encompassment is from the perspective of being a subject (من حيث الموضوعية), i.e., as something investigated in the science. The author did not merely say 'the subject encompasses His essence, attributes, and actions' but added 'investigations' (مباحث) to emphasize that the encompassment is from the investigative perspective, which is the true basis of honor. An analogy: grammar encompasses God's speech and the Prophet's speech, but that does not make grammar nobler than tafsir or hadith; the honor comes from the mode of investigation. Thus, the subject matter of kalam is both the most general (making it nobler by its inclusivity) and the noblest in itself (because it treats the highest realities). The science is therefore honored in both ways.

Key Terms
فيتناول
أعم الأمور
أعلاها
مباحث
مسائل
شرافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that simply stating that the subject matter includes God's essence, attributes, and actions automatically makes kalam the noblest science.
Correction: The objections show that the relationship between subject and problems, and the perspective of honor, must be carefully distinguished.

Checkpoint
Which objection argues that the statement about the 'highest' is unnecessary because the subject is already 'most general'?
A) First objection
B) Second objection
C) Third objection
D) Fourth objection

Key Takeaway
The four objections reveal critical logical issues in the claim that kalam's subject matter directly proves its honor: redundancy, category confusion, misattribution of honor, and perspective mismatch.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you assert the superiority of Islamic knowledge over other sciences, are you relying on its subject being 'the most general' or on the actual content of your knowledge? Which of these truly transforms your heart? If it's the former, you are guilty of the first objection—redundancy. Are you comfortable with that?
?
The second objection reveals a category mistake: mixing the subject of a science with its problems. In your personal study of Islam, do you ever confuse the framework (e.g., categories of kalam) with the actual questions you need to answer? Could this confusion be hiding a lack of depth? Take a moment to identify one area where you might be mixing subject and problem.
?
The fourth objection points out a mismatch: proving honor from the known object rather than the subject. In your daily life, are you more concerned with the honor of the knowledge you possess (what you know) or the honor of the One you know (the subject of that knowledge)? If you find yourself boasting about your knowledge, you have shifted perspective. Will you realign your intention today?

Resolving the Objections: The True Basis of Kalam's Honor
Detailed resolution of the four objections with reinterpretation and analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the response to the objections reframes the issue: the honor comes from the investigative mode, not mere subject generality.

Core Idea
Honor lies in the investigative perspective, not in mere enumeration of topics.

After hearing the objections, the response clarifies the precise meaning of the statements. By interpreting 'higher' as 'nobler' and emphasizing the 'investigative' perspective, the response preserves the claim that kalam is the noblest science. This lesson unpacks the sophisticated resolution.

Guided Path
1
Read the response passage
Read the Arabic passage containing the interpretation and analogy. Notice how each objection is addressed implicitly or explicitly.
2
Understand the reinterpretation
The response reinterprets 'higher' as 'nobler' and explains the role of the 'fa' and the implicit pronoun. Focus on how this changes the meaning.
3
Analyze the analogy with grammar
The example of grammar encompassing God's speech is key. Why doesn't that make grammar nobler? This illustrates the need for the investigative perspective.
4
Grasp the two grounds of honor
The response concludes that kalam's subject is both most general (honor by inclusivity) and noblest in itself (honor by content). See how these two reasons work together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فيتناول) إلخ فيه اختلال من وجوه أما أولاً فلأنه لا حاجة إلى هذا التفريع بعد التصريح بأن موضوعه أعم الأمور أي الموضوعات لما تقرر أن العلوم تتصاعد بتصاعد الموضوعات عموماً وخصوصاً، وأما ثانياً فلان مباحث ذاته تعالى وصفاته وأفعاله من المسائل ولا معنى لتناول الموضوع للمسائل، وأما ثالثاً فلان على صحته يفيد إثبات شرافة الموضوع وأما رابعاً فلان قوله لا شك إنه إذا كان المعلوم إلخ يفيد إثبات شرافة العلم باعتبار معلومه والمقصود إثبات شرافته باعتبار موضوعه وغاية التوجيه أنه قدس سره حمل الأعلى على معنى الأشرف، لا على الأعلى رتبة ليكون تأسيساً، والفاء في قوله فيتناول تعليلية أو استئنافية أو زائدة والجملة تعليل لكونه أشرف الموضوعات، والضمير المستتر راجع إلى موضوعه وقيد الحيثية ملحوظ أي لأنه يتناول موضوعه من حيث أنه موضوع أي مبحوث عنه في العلم أشرف المعلومات التي هي ذاته تعالى وصفاته وأفعاله من حيث كونها مبحوثاً عنها ولم يكتف بتناوله للأمور الثلاثة من حيث أنفسها لأنه لا يفيد شرافة العلم، ألا ترى أن موضوع النحو يتناول كلامه تعالى وكلام الرسول، ولا يلزم منه أشرفيته من علم التفسير والحديث، وللإشارة إلى كون التناول من حيث البحث محط الشرافة قدم لفظ المباحث، فالحاصل أن موضوع الكلام أعم الموضوعات فيكون أشرف لأن العلوم تتصاعد بتصاعد الموضوعات، وأن موضوعه أشرف الموضوعات لتناوله ذاته وصفاته وأفعاله التي هي أشرف المعلومات، ولا شك أن المعلوم الذي هو الموضوع إذا كان أشرف بسبب ذلك التناول كان العلم المتعلق به أي الباحث عن أحواله أشرف وخلاصته إثبات شرافة موضوعه باعتبار شموله للموضوعات، وباعتباره في نفسه ولذا عبر عن الموضوع في قوله ولا شك إلخ بالمعلوم.
His saying: 'so it encompasses' etc. There is in it a disorder from several aspects. First: there is no need for this branching after the explicit statement that its subject is the most general of matters, i.e., of subjects, because it is established that sciences ascend with the ascending of subjects in generality and specificity. Second: the investigations of His essence, attributes, and actions are from among the problems, and there is no meaning to the subject encompassing the problems. Third: if it is correct, it would prove the honor of the subject. Fourth: his saying 'there is no doubt that when the known is nobler' etc. proves the honor of the science in consideration of its known object, but the intention is to prove its honor in consideration of its subject. The ultimate interpretation is that he, may God sanctify his secret, interpreted 'higher' in the sense of 'nobler', not in the sense of 'higher in rank', so that it would be an original point. The 'fa' in his saying 'so it encompasses' is explanatory, or resumptive, or redundant, and the sentence is an explanation of its being the noblest of subjects. The implicit pronoun refers to its subject, and the restriction of 'from where it is a subject' is taken into account, i.e., because it encompasses its subject from the perspective that it is a subject, i.e., investigated in the science, the noblest of known things, which are His essence, attributes, and actions from the aspect that they are investigated. He did not content himself with its encompassing the three things from the aspect of themselves because that would not entail the honor of the science. Do you not see that the subject of grammar encompasses the speech of God and the speech of the Messenger, yet it does not follow that it is nobler than the science of exegesis and hadith? And to indicate that the encompassing from the perspective of investigation is the locus of honor, he introduced the word 'investigations'. The upshot is that the subject of kalam is the most general of subjects, so it is nobler because sciences ascend with the ascending of subjects, and its subject is the noblest of subjects because it encompasses His essence, attributes, and actions which are the noblest of known things. There is no doubt that when the known which is the subject is nobler due to that encompassing, the science related to it — i.e., that which investigates its states — is nobler. The summary is the proof of the honor of its subject in consideration of its including subjects, and in consideration of itself. For that reason he expressed the subject in his saying 'there is no doubt' etc. as 'the known'.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. It begins by presenting four objections to the earlier claim that the subject matter of kalam encompasses the noblest known things (God's essence, attributes, actions) and thereby demonstrates the science's honor. The first objection: since it was already stated that the subject is the most general of matters, the additional statement that it is the highest (أعلاها) is redundant — generality already implies superiority. Second: the investigations (مباحث) of God's essence, etc. are actually the problems (مسائل) of the science, not part of the subject; a subject does not encompass its own problems. Third: even if it did encompass them, it would only prove the honor of the subject, not of the science itself. Fourth: the later statement 'when the known is nobler, the science is nobler' proves honor from the perspective of the known object (المعلوم), but the goal here is to prove honor from the perspective of the subject (موضوع). The answer resolves each point. The author explains that the word 'highest' (أعلاها) is interpreted as 'noblest' (أشرف), not 'higher in rank' (أعلى رتبة), to make an original point. The 'fa' in 'فيتناول' can be explanatory or resumptive, and the entire clause is an explanation that the subject is the noblest of subjects. The implicit pronoun in 'يتناول' refers to the subject, and the encompassment is from the perspective of being a subject (من حيث الموضوعية), i.e., as something investigated in the science. The author did not merely say 'the subject encompasses His essence, attributes, and actions' but added 'investigations' (مباحث) to emphasize that the encompassment is from the investigative perspective, which is the true basis of honor. An analogy: grammar encompasses God's speech and the Prophet's speech, but that does not make grammar nobler than tafsir or hadith; the honor comes from the mode of investigation. Thus, the subject matter of kalam is both the most general (making it nobler by its inclusivity) and the noblest in itself (because it treats the highest realities). The science is therefore honored in both ways.

Key Terms
الأعلى
الأشرف
فيتناول
تعليلية
استئنافية
مباحث
من حيث الموضوعية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that simply including God's essence in the subject matter suffices for honor, regardless of how it is investigated.
Correction: The response shows that the honor comes from the investigative mode (mabahith), not just the content.

Checkpoint
According to the response, why does grammar's inclusion of God's speech not make grammar nobler than tafsir?
A) Because grammar does not investigate God's speech as divine revelation
B) Because grammar's subject is not the most general
C) Because grammar only covers linguistic aspects, not theological
D) Because grammar is a lower science

Key Takeaway
The response restores the claim of kalam's honor by clarifying that the encompassing is from the investigative perspective, and the subject is both most general and noblest in itself.

The Three Aspects of Honor for Kalam
The author identifies the three sources of honor for kalam and declares it most honorable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three criteria that determine the honor of a science and why kalam is considered the most honorable.

Core Idea
The honor of a science rests on its object, goal, and proof — and kalam excels in all three.

This passage from al-Mawaqif establishes a key principle: a science's honor is not arbitrary but based on three measurable aspects. By examining these, we can see why kalam is uniquely noble. This lesson unpacks each aspect and the conclusion drawn.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its literal translation. Let the author's wording settle before analyzing.
Pay attention to the three terms he lists.
2
Identify the three aspects of honor
The passage explicitly names three aspects: the object of study (معلومه), the goal (غايته), and the proof (حجته). Notice how these encompass all aspects of honor.
These are the criteria for evaluating any science.
3
Understand the author's emphasis on comprehensiveness
The author stresses that these three aspects do not exceed the possible aspects of honor. He also notes that the excellence of a science's issues relates to the reliability of its proofs.
This underlines the completeness of the criteria.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that kalam is the most honorable science according to all aspects of honor. Ask yourself why that must be true given the three criteria.
Consider the object (Allah), goal (felicity), and proof (decisive arguments) of kalam.

المرصد الأول - المقصد الخامس : مسائله التي هي المقاصد علم الكلام أعني معلومه وغايته وحجته ( هي جهات شرف العلم لا تعدوها ) أي لا تتجاوز جهات الشرف هذه الأمور التي ذكرناها ، وأما كون مسائل العلم [؟] أقوم [؟] فراجع إلى فضيلة الدلائل ووثاقتها ( فهو ) فالكلام ( إذا أشرف العلوم بحسب جميع جهات الشرف .

And as for the issues of the science being 'more upright' (?), that refers to the excellence of its proofs and their reliability. (Therefore) kalam (is) indeed the most honorable of sciences with respect to all aspects of honor.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This is a declarative passage establishing the honor of the science of kalam. The author first identifies the three aspects that confer honor upon any science: its object of study (معلومه), its goal (غايته), and its proof (حجته). He emphasizes that these three encompass all aspects of honor and do not exceed them. Then he notes that the issues (مسائل) of a science, when they are 'more upright' (أقوم) [possibly a variant reading], relate to the excellence and reliability of its proofs. Consequently, kalam qualifies as the most honorable science when measured by all these aspects.

What is a Mas'ala? The Definition and Its Nuances
Definition of mas'ala as theoretical judgment with nuance for necessary judgments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the scholars of kalam define a 'mas'ala' (problem) and why the description 'theoretical' is dominant but not exclusive.

Core Idea
A problem in kalam is primarily a theoretical judgment, but it can also be necessary if it needs clarification.

Before we dive into the architecture of kalam, we must first understand its basic building blocks: the problems (masa'il) it studies. This passage clarifies what scholars mean by 'mas'ala' and why they emphasize its theoretical nature, while acknowledging that some problems may be necessary. Let's explore how this definition sets the stage for kalam's methodology.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of mas'ala
The passage begins with the statement that a mas'ala is 'every theoretical judgment.' Read carefully: the problem itself is identified with the judgment because the judgment is what is sought in the science.
Notice that the sides of the proposition (subject and predicate) are considered conceptual principles, not the problem itself.
2
Examine the exception for necessary judgments
The description 'theoretical' is based on the majority of cases. The passage notes that a problem may also be necessary, but it is still included in the science either because it needs a reminder or to explain its 'why'.
This shows that kalam's scope includes some self-evident truths that require elaboration.
3
Understand the outcome of the definition
The commentator then explains why every theoretical judgment is interpreted as a problem: they are ultimately about religious beliefs or things on which their proof depends.
This connects the definition to the purpose of kalam: defending and establishing religious doctrines.
4
Reflect on the key insight
Notice that the problem is the judgment itself, not its components. This focus on the judgment as the unit of analysis is foundational for kalam's logical structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام ( كل حكم نظري جعل المسألة نفس الحكم لأنه المقصود في القضية المطلوبة في العلم ، وأما أطرافه فمن المبادي التصورية، ووصف الحكم بكونه نظرياً بناء على الغالب، وإلا فالمسألة قد تكون ضرورية، فتورد في العلم، إما لاحتياجها إلى تنبيه يزيل عنها خفاءها أو لبيان لميتها وإنما حمل كل حكم نظري على المسائل نظراً إلى مآل معناه كأنه قال : وهي الأحكام النظرية لمعلوم هو ) أي ذلك الحكم النظري ( من العقائد الدينية، أو يتوقف عليه إثبات شيء منها ) سواء كان توقفاً قريباً أو بعيداً (وهو) أي الكلام ( العلم الأعلى إليه تنتهي العلوم الشرعية كلها، وفيه تثبت موضوعاتها أو حيثياتها فليست له مباد تبين في علم (آخر) سواء كان علماً شرعياً، أو غير شرعي وذلك أن علماء الإسلام قد دونوا لإثبات العقائد الدينية المتعلقة بالصانع تعالى وصفاته وأفعاله وما يتفرع عليها من مباحث النبوة، والمعاد علماً يتوصل به إلى إعلاء كلمة الحق فيها، ولم يرضوا أن يكونوا محتاجين فيه إلى علم آخر أصلا، فأخذوا موضوعه على وجه يتناول تلك العقائد والمباحث النظرية التي تتوقف عليها تلك العقائد سواء كان توقفها عليها باعتبار مواد أدلتها، أو باعتبار صورها، وجعلوا جميع ذلك مقاصد مطلوبة في علمهم هذا فجاء علماً مستغنياً في

قوله : ( نفس الحكم أي الوقوع لا الإيقاع لأن المسألة من المعلومات . قوله : (أو لبيان لميتها فإن قلت لميتها إذا كانت نظرية كانت بهذا الاعتبار داخلة في قياسات العلم، ولا تكون بينة بذاتها بل هي مسلمة بحسن الظن والتصديق بهلية موضوع الكلام والإلهي مثلا بديهي كما ذكره الشارح سابقاً فكيف يحكم بكون هلية الموضوع من الأصول الموضوعة مطلقاً اللهم إلا أن يحمل على التغليب .

قوله : ( وفيه تثبت موضوعاتها أو حيثياتها أي إن احتيج إلى الإثبات فلا نقض بالعربية ومثل إثبات حيثية الموضوع في الكلام إثبات الصحة وعدمها التي هي حيثية الأعمال، التي هي موضوع الفقه فيه فإن إثبات صحة الأعمال وفسادها إنما يكون بالقرآن والحديث، وإثباتهما يكون في هذا الفن.

قوله : فليس له مباد تبين في علم (آخر هذا التفريع إنما يتم على زعم المصنف وإلا فقد صرح الشارح فيما سبق بأن مبادي العلم الأعلى قد تبين في علم أدنى وإن كان على قلة فمجرد كون الكلام علماً على حدة لا يستتبع أن لا تكون له مباد مبينة في علم آخر، اللهم إلا أن يلاحظ ما ذكره الشارح من البيان أو يلحق النادر بالمعدوم وفيه ما فيه قوله: (وجعلوا جميع ذلك مقاصد مطلوبة إلخ) فيه بحث لأن هذا الكلام مخالف لما ذكره في حواشي شرح المختصر حيث قال والحق أن إثبات مسائل العلوم النظرية يحتاج إلى
The speech: (Every theoretical judgment) making the problem itself the judgment because it is the intended in the sought proposition in the science. As for its sides, they are from the conceptual principles. The description of the judgment as theoretical is based on the majority, otherwise the problem may be necessary, and it is presented in the science either because it needs a reminder that removes its hiddenness or to explain its why. And he only interpreted every theoretical judgment as referring to the problems with a view to the outcome of its meaning, as if he said: they are the theoretical judgments for a known (i.e., that theoretical judgment) from the religious beliefs, or something from them depends on its establishment (whether the dependence is close or far). And it (i.e., kalam) is the highest science to which all the religious sciences end, and in it their subjects or their aspects are established, so it has no principles explained in another science, whether it is a religious science or non-religious. That is because the scholars of Islam have recorded a science for establishing the religious beliefs related to the Maker, Exalted, His attributes, His actions, and what branches from them of the investigations of prophethood and the return, a science by which the word of truth in them is raised, and they were not willing to be in need of another science at all. So they took its subject in a way that encompasses those beliefs and the theoretical investigations on which those beliefs depend, whether their dependence on them is with regard to the materials of their proofs or with regard to their forms, and they made all of that sought purposes in this their science, so it became a science independent in itself.

His statement: (The judgment itself) meaning the occurrence, not the causing, because the problem is among the knowns. His statement: (Or to explain its why) for if you say: its why, if it is theoretical, it is in this respect included in the syllogisms of the science, and it is not evident by itself, but is accepted by good assumption and affirmation. The hiyya (existence) of the subject of kalam and the divine, for example, is self-evident as the commentator mentioned previously. So how can it be judged that the hiyya of the subject is among the postulated principles absolutely? Unless it is interpreted as a preponderance.

His statement: (And in it their subjects or their aspects are established) i.e., if proof is needed, then there is no objection from Arabic and the like. An example is the establishment of the aspect of the subject in kalam: the establishment of validity and its absence, which is the aspect of actions, which is the subject of jurisprudence in it. For the establishment of the validity of actions and their corruption is only by the Quran and Hadith, and their establishment is in this art.

His statement: (So it has no principles explained in another science) this deduction is only valid according to the opinion of the author. Otherwise, the commentator has stated previously that the principles of the highest science may be explained in a lower science, even if rarely. So merely that kalam is a separate science does not imply that it has no principles explained in another science. Unless one considers what the commentator mentioned of the explanation, or joins the rare with the non-existent, and in it is what is in it. His statement: (And they made all of that sought purposes, etc.) in it there is discussion because this statement contradicts what he mentioned in the footnotes of Sharh al-Mukhtasar, where he said: 'And the truth is that the establishment of problems of the theoretical sciences needs...'
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This lesson defines the 'masa'il' (problems) of kalam. The passage begins with the statement that a problem is 'every theoretical judgment,' making the problem itself the judgment because the judgment is what is sought. The sides of the proposition are conceptual principles. The description 'theoretical' is dominant, but problems can be necessary if they need clarification of their why. The commentator interprets 'every theoretical judgment' as referring to religious beliefs or things on which their proof depends. Then he declares that kalam is the highest science (al-'ilm al-a'la), to which all religious sciences end, and in kalam their subjects or aspects are established, so it has no principles from another science. This is because Islamic scholars founded kalam to establish beliefs about God, His attributes, actions, prophethood, and the afterlife, and they made it self-sufficient by including all necessary materials and forms of proof. The commentary then explains specific phrases: 'the judgment itself' means the occurrence, not the causing; 'or to explain its why' raises the issue that if a problem's why is theoretical, it is part of the syllogisms and not self-evident, yet the existence of kalam's subject is self-evident. Regarding 'in it their subjects or aspects are established,' it gives the example of validity of actions in jurisprudence, which are established by Quran and Hadith within kalam. The final part discusses the claim that kalam has no principles from another science, noting that this depends on the author's view; the commentator previously said that the highest science's principles may be explained in a lower science, and merely being separate does not preclude borrowing. The lesson ends with a note that the statement about making all sought purposes contradicts the commentator's own footnote in Sharh al-Mukhtasar.

الحكم النظري
المبادي التصورية
الضرورية

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All problems in kalam are purely theoretical and cannot be necessary.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that while most problems are theoretical, some may be necessary. They are included to remove hiddenness or explain their rationale.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why might a necessary problem still be taught in the science of kalam?
A) Because it is theoretical
B) Because it needs a reminder or to explain its why
C) Because it is not part of the science

Key Takeaway
A mas'ala is primarily a theoretical judgment, but kalam also treats necessary judgments when they need clarification or explanation of their rationale.
